<div id="review_1768444215" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1768444215" />
    <a title="Ann Girdharry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13002277-ann-girdharry"><img alt="Ann Girdharry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444634224p2/13002277.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1768444215?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann Girdharry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann Girdharry" href="/user/show/13002277-ann-girdharry">Ann Girdharry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13002277-ann-girdharry?shelf=new-authors-of-colour">new-authors-of-colour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13002277-ann-girdharry?shelf=my-challenge-authors-of-colour">my-challenge-authors-of-colour</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1768444215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16173707425766365373">This is the story of two young girls from the same family, who grow up to be women in Afghanistan - Shekiba and Rahima. The girls lived generations apart and so the story is told in two different times but with very similar experiences for each girl - the experience of a terrifying marriage as a child, the abuse of family-in-laws, the harshness and punishing attitude of their 'husbands', forced sex and rape, the drudgery and emptiness of their lives, their lowly status as women in a society that</span>
  <span id="freeText16173707425766365373" style="display:none">This is the story of two young girls from the same family, who grow up to be women in Afghanistan - Shekiba and Rahima. The girls lived generations apart and so the story is told in two different times but with very similar experiences for each girl - the experience of a terrifying marriage as a child, the abuse of family-in-laws, the harshness and punishing attitude of their 'husbands', forced sex and rape, the drudgery and emptiness of their lives, their lowly status as women in a society that values men. There are a few brighter moments but there is much tragedy - the death of siblings, the death of children, the death of loved relatives, the death of all hope, and both women have times when they yearn for death as a way out. <br />I enjoyed learning about the culture of Shekiba and Rahima and this window on their lives, whilst harrowing, was also enlightening. In addition, the story gives insight into some of the political changes that Afghanistan underwent, mirrored in the girls' lives. <br />The only thing I wanted more of, was more of a sense of intimacy with Shekiba and Rahima. They were both incredibly strong young women, and I would have liked to know them better. <br /><br />For a wonderful interview with Nadia Hashimi, see <br /><i> Five Things You Didn't Know about Nadia Hashimi</i> <br />over on my blog.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://anngirdharry.weebly.com/blog/3-discover-ten-new-authors-of-colour">http://anngirdharry.weebly.com/blog/3...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16173707425766365373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2130802260" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2130802260" />
    <a title="Kavita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5858699-kavita"><img alt="Kavita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1315387023p2/5858699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2130802260?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kavita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kavita" href="/user/show/5858699-kavita">Kavita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5858699-kavita?shelf=afghanistan">afghanistan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2130802260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4742160670815312314">In a remote village in Afghanistan, Rahima is growing up with a bunch of sisters. When her mother realises there are not going to be any sons, she decides to take the advice of her rebel sister and make one of her daughters into a son. Following the age-old tradition of <i>bacha posh</i>, Rahima became Rahim and began to act like a boy, receiving all the benefits that a patriarchal system bestows on humans born with penises. But what Rahima does not realise that she would have to become a woman again e</span>
  <span id="freeText4742160670815312314" style="display:none">In a remote village in Afghanistan, Rahima is growing up with a bunch of sisters. When her mother realises there are not going to be any sons, she decides to take the advice of her rebel sister and make one of her daughters into a son. Following the age-old tradition of <i>bacha posh</i>, Rahima became Rahim and began to act like a boy, receiving all the benefits that a patriarchal system bestows on humans born with penises. But what Rahima does not realise that she would have to become a woman again eventually.<br /><br />The book was an interesting look at the way extremely patriarchal societies allow women to choose to be a man. These girls then gain respect in society and are allowed a lot of freedoms. The other way around is also possible when young boys are turned into girls. This custom is known as <i>bacha bazi</i> in Afghanistan and the young boys are then sexually exploited. Basically, being male brings freedom and being female brings humiliation and exploitation.<br /><br />The book explores life in remote Afghanistan and there are two parallel stories. While Rahima struggles to make sense of her life, she unearths the story of her ancestor, Shekiba, who was also a bit of a rebel in her time. I found Shekiba's story the more interesting because of the historical context. <br /><br />Nadia Hashimi makes the same mistake that many Afghan Americans novelists make - she paints life in Afghanistan as one single round of constant misery day in and day out. There were never any happy times when the characters were actually content and happy. It got a bit annoying after a while to read about Rahima whining about her life continuously. <br /><br />The book also left both stories slightly unfinished. After grumbling and moaning for pages, the characters were suddenly content at the end because politics happened (in Shekiba's case). Rahima's story was left unfinished as far as I am concerned. Certain incidents in her life that make it possible for Rahima to escape also appeared to be too convenient. In real cases, it's never that easy.<br /><br />This is a pretty decent book in many ways and the author has definitely done her research, but it could have done with a bit of polishing and addition of a few happy moments.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4742160670815312314" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_914267524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/914267524" />
    <a title="Pamela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20048096-pamela"><img alt="Pamela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598408667p2/20048096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/914267524?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela" href="/user/show/20048096-pamela">Pamela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=culture">culture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=top-picks-read-in-2013-2014">top-picks-read-in-2013-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=womens-fiction">womens-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=middle-east">middle-east</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20048096-pamela?shelf=controversial-topics">controversial-topics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer914267524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16532037103783110400">Beautifully and compassionately written, “The Pearl that Broke Its Shell” is a heart-wrenching yet hopeful story exemplifying the oppressive, unjust and often brutal realities of women in Afghanistan. Nadia Hashimi has penned a masterpiece. And though it’s a lengthy read, it is well worth the vested time. <br/><br/>The multi-generational stories of Rahima and Shekiba brought to light elements of Afghani laws, customs, and traditions that were relatively unknown to me: Women are entitled to inherit land an</span>
  <span id="freeText16532037103783110400" style="display:none">Beautifully and compassionately written, “The Pearl that Broke Its Shell” is a heart-wrenching yet hopeful story exemplifying the oppressive, unjust and often brutal realities of women in Afghanistan. Nadia Hashimi has penned a masterpiece. And though it’s a lengthy read, it is well worth the vested time. <br /><br />The multi-generational stories of Rahima and Shekiba brought to light elements of Afghani laws, customs, and traditions that were relatively unknown to me: Women are entitled to inherit land and vote – however, laws are rarely acknowledge impartially or applied equitably as opium lords and warlords reign supreme with iron fists; a prescribed number of women are required to be seated in parliament – however, they are rarely called on in assembly to speak, and they are generally nothing more than puppets; And households where no son resides, a young daughter may become a ‘bocha posh’ (a girl posing as a boy until menses) in order to perform male duties for the household, unrestricted by female servitude/chattel rules. <br /> <br />"This life is difficult. We lose fathers, brothers, mothers, songbirds, and pieces of ourselves. Whips strike the innocent, honors go to the guilty, and there is too much loneliness . . . But I can pray for small things, like fertile fields, a mother's love, a child's smile - a life that's less bitter than sweet."<br /><br />This hauntingly powerful novel will linger long in my heart, mind, and prayers. My heart breaks with thoughts of the rampant generational anger and greed-driven hostilities and corruption in much of the Middle East region. It has certainly given me a greater appreciation for freedoms, privileges, and opportunities inherently afforded me as a born and bred American citizen. May the women of Afghanistan one day rise above gender bias and oppression, and come to know true freedom and the God of love, mercy, joy, and peace.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16532037103783110400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1947508645" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2099130-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271260338p2/2099130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1947508645?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/2099130-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1947508645" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer529072798984352442">Yes, she is now your brother Rahim. You will forget about your sister Rahima and welcome your brother."<br/><br/>With that Rahima's mother begins reorienting Rahima's sisters to Rahim. She has begun her life as a bachem posh, a girl assuming the identity of a boy. This is an ancient Afghani custom which allows a girl to live as a boy until she reaches puberty. Because of all the restrictions placed on females in their society, Rahima welcomes the new freedoms she has as a boy. <br/><br/>Rahima's story is skillfully</span>
  <span id="freeText529072798984352442" style="display:none">Yes, she is now your brother Rahim. You will forget about your sister Rahima and welcome your brother."<br /><br />With that Rahima's mother begins reorienting Rahima's sisters to Rahim. She has begun her life as a bachem posh, a girl assuming the identity of a boy. This is an ancient Afghani custom which allows a girl to live as a boy until she reaches puberty. Because of all the restrictions placed on females in their society, Rahima welcomes the new freedoms she has as a boy. <br /><br />Rahima's story is skillfully interwoven with that of her great-great grandmother Shekiba who shared a similar story. Nadia Hashimi brings to life the hardships of being a woman in Afghanistan by telling us the stories of these two amazing women. If you thought life was bad for women there, this book will only reinforce this belief by giving you a detailed picture of what that life is like. Even in translation, this book is replete with beautiful imagery and language. It's a must read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="529072798984352442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2835945758" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2835945758" />
    <a title="Monika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38021482-monika"><img alt="Monika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581038684p2/38021482.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2835945758?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monika" href="/user/show/38021482-monika">Monika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062244765" href="/book/show/18735908-the-pearl-that-broke-its-shell">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2835945758" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16204927516739482866">I haven't seen a real pearl yet. I don't know if it would be slippery to my fingers or if it would transport me to sandy beaches. I don't know how the pearl convinced a shell to protect it from the world. I don't know how a shell would feel if a prying hand reaches it and tries to take out the pearl it is so longingly protecting. I might not know a lot of things but this I know - a pearl breaking its shell has to be the most breathtaking sight ever. It doesn't matter if it is the real pearl or a</span>
  <span id="freeText16204927516739482866" style="display:none">I haven't seen a real pearl yet. I don't know if it would be slippery to my fingers or if it would transport me to sandy beaches. I don't know how the pearl convinced a shell to protect it from the world. I don't know how a shell would feel if a prying hand reaches it and tries to take out the pearl it is so longingly protecting. I might not know a lot of things but this I know - a pearl breaking its shell has to be the most breathtaking sight ever. It doesn't matter if it is the real pearl or a pearl appearing like animals or human beings . . . particularly the oppressed, who continue to be neglected and are often raided off. <br /><br />Set as a two-dimensional family saga, <i>The Pearl That Broke Its Shell</i> is about continuously conflicting emotions. Liberated and enslaved, finding voice and remaining voiceless, an upliftment because of culture and degradation due to it and so on. The tale spans across two centuries, but so does the condition. Shunning years of patriarchal system won't do, it is internalisation that also needs to be curbed. Men aren't the only ones who try to keep women in their holds, it is also women who specialise in power and who are also able to find their prey. <br /><br />The novel is pretty simple in terms of language. Don't let this illusion of simplicity act as a deterrent. This book will stay with you. It will remain close to your heart as long as power hierarchy exists in the world. I am not aiming to glorify what it is not, but I certainly feel that it has the potential to be one of the stepping stones to the road of freedom, love and peace (provided climate crisis doesn't kill us before we are able to reach our one true home).</span>
  <a data-text-id="16204927516739482866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N1RuTSAr4OgKHEEmDa6WTwhLKCpjhNhxWs1X2rOxMRwzVZiVelfRR96kuCB3CXqfEaCgF8h8maq7jy0wdbxSeg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('il32CPF63qnAowVjdvk1Cgt5+RK/x+4NY4JdtahN4m+OXADQqwbvBhQb/GUMXtnaEpJxLxQ/r9aCwCdfbkCBCQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

For Lavinia and Juneau Jane, the journey is one of inheritance and financial desperation, but for Hannie, torn from her mother and eight siblings before slavery\'s end, the pilgrimage westward reignites an agonizing question: Could her long-lost family still be out there?
